It looks great visually! I can't wait to play the completed map. If you're going for immersion, though, there's a few things you'll need to make it believable that this is a lived in town. You'll need a schoolhouse, a town hall for government and judicial proceedings (a place and people to decide the laws and judge the accused in jail) and the town meetings; and a stable bedside the blacksmith for all the animals needed to move and feed the people. It's beside the blacksmith for ferrier services (the one to trim and care for hooves and shoe them). Animals typically turn the cranks to lift  loads up and down the cliff faces. They can also work the mill when there's intermittent wind or lacking a water wheel (even with a water wheel then the stream/river is low). Otherwise, I don't see a food source for the people. Grain and hay needed for the animals, and I assume the people aren't carnivores, so some for them as well nearby. People will never set down roots in a place that can't sustain them. Old West towns always had nearby farms. You can't assume a saloon depends 100% on trade; if it's as old as it looks to be, they'll have a distillery, for which one requires grain at least. Don't forget a few town wells to water everything and everyone. Those will be nice touches for realism.  There are different types of deserts. In SoCal, I grew up surrounded by chaparral deserts. There's lots of dry mesic chaparral all up and down CA. If there's enough water for chaparral, you can grow crops if you irritate well. I used to eat the sour wine grapes of long-neglected vineyards and enjoyed near-wild citrus fruits.

Story Idea: During the times of war, the Ultimate Survival World possessed two beings. These individuals could be responsible for the inevitable convergence that has been melded from the roots below. This world is almost trapped in time, consisting of ten biomes.  Among the snowy mountain, there had been a secret crystal that completely enveloped the grass lands prior. However, there was a reason for this. To stop the corruption of The End from spreading, The Queen of The Icy Mountain had to steal the knowledge from the dark oak forest's mansion, and take advantage from the wizards. Then, she had to envelop her nation into complete frost. She was the main reason why time had stopped and only two daylight cycles remained. This Island is the remnants of her actions. Though everyone hated her, she was the main reason why The Calamity hadn't started.  The Nether was so close to ordering the Onslaught, that deep underground, they almost destroyed the Roots of below. When The Queen of The Ice Nation vanished, she dispersed all her magical power through the world to keep it from dying. She wasn't a villain, rather a hero.

I grew up in what used to be a western town in Oregon and you can really tell in some parts of the town. The oldest buildings are obviously scattered like the image provided but downtown the buildings are right next to each other like in the movies. Including old buildings like the bank. You can really see where the dirt roads used to be. We also have a train track running through that part of town alongside a water tower and a large mysterious "W" on one of the, now to be, tattoo shops that really helps you imagine what things used to look like. After a great flood they began to expand the town from what is considered "down town" and even 100 years later we still have town events like the hops and heritage festival or Saturday market. Only now with canopies instead of tents and stakes. The town of Independence Oregon has a lot of history, Lewis and Clark traveled through our town as it was part of the Oregon Trail and is considered today to be the third largest urban area in Polk County.

Here's some ideas for the taiga area: I think the taiga village should be inspired by Russian architecture. Considering the snowy forests and everything, I think basing it off of Russia would be really cool, and it would also be a really good chance to make an awesome orthodox-style cathedral.   On top of that, another idea is that the taiga settlement could actually be more like a proper city rather than a small village. Considering that there are shipwrecks scattered around the island, that means that someone had to have built them at some point, and the island needs to have a proper trading center where all the peoples of the island can go to trade and access the outside world. That's why I think the Taiga settlement should be an actual city, as it would be the only place where the islanders have trade access to the outside world, and would have shipbuilding drydocks capable of launching those large ships that we've seen in the form of several shipwrecks.  If you choose to take this route and make the Taiga settlement a city, then lore-wise, it could be that after the jungle city and civilization fell into ruin, the peoples of the taiga overtook the status as premier civilization on the island, developing a large city to replace the now abandoned jungle city as the main trading center on the island.

3:39 - In the old west, a leatherworker would have been, along with the blacksmith's, at the local stable .  His business would've been called the saddlery, where he sold saddles and tack (leather harnesses, straps, et cetera). 3:58 - Everyone knows the jail is in the back of the Sheriff's office.  Otherwise, how are the sheriff and deputy/deputies supposed to keep an eye on the prisoners? 5:29 - You forgot the school.  The schoolteacher would have to live somewhere other than the school. You also forgot the doctor's office, the general store, the feed and grain store (likely near the stable), the assayer's office (since there WILL be miners in the area), and the post office. 10:18 - Buildings on stilts such as that would have been massively impractical and, as far as I know, it was NEVER done.  Nor were cranes.  Ore was packed onto mules and "mule trains" walked up narrow trails, if it needed to be brought out of canyons.

While yeah 16,000,000 blocks seems HUGE, you really need to put it into perspective to see how big it actually is! Minecraft world span about 30,000,000 blocks (although with commands it can be higher), most people don't travel past 20,000 blocks from spawn. Also, 1 minecraft block = 1 meter (3.28 feet) in the real world, 16,000,000 meters is bigger than some countries!

yoooooooo theres another one out!  edit: I just realized something, but first you'll need some background. In my school the orchestra class has this thing that we do called orchestraland, and we have a bunch of characters and all that in it, but the layout of the room and our drawings of orchestraland are almost exactly the same as the layout of this world. The right of the room holds violin volcano and violin village, violin volcano is essentially a wasteland because of a recent eruption so the desert and mesa fit that well, and violin village works well with the mesa village that you make in this video. the middle area is viola valley, and while there isn't a valley, the area around the valley is essentially a plains, as well as there being a river flowing through it. to the right of the room is cello forest and that also fits in pretty well to where the jungle is, as well as the jungle temple fitting almost perfectly to the position of the bass base I.R.L. and finally the dark oak forest is directly in the correct place to be the forbidden forest, the forbidden forest isn't connected to the mainland, but there's also an evil presence in there, and a league of villains (you might consider a family) that had there base set up there but mysteriously disappeared. the island is even in the exact same shape.

Trixy, this project was really nice at the start. You are a great builder and have a lot of good ideas. But you could really do with asking someone else who isnt part of the project to look over how immersive your ideas really are. Cause lemme be real with you, a lot of them are just not.  At the start it was really cool, but the more and more you go into it, the more it feels like you are giving areas attention based on how you feel and not on what they need You go for looks over immersivenes, which is the complete oposite of what you are aiming for. The Desert Pyramid was one thing. The Forestvillage another. The Mansion too has a lack of space and dont get me started on the jungle ruins.  Now you come to this desert town and you not only give us once again a barely established town that is somehow capable of having a full on propped up bank and hotel but at the same time they couldnt afford to get a stonemade church? You know what you based this off of right? On a USA culture that was heavily christianized, meaning if they have made anything out of stone before any other business it was the church. And also the churche is usually not in the middle of the town like this either. But that isnt the only issue. You got a lot of stores in that village, which on its own is fine, but... where are the people that live there? If the storeowners supposedly buy from one another, the towns gonna be broke real quick, no matter how neat the lore is. Where are the other houses? Of mine workers and farmers and whatnot?  Oh and another thing: Where did they get spruce wood from in a Mesa Biome? Dont give me the "From the Taiga Forest" answer, thats obvious. But then they also would have brought over seedlings. You see what I mean? Your lore can be neat and everything, but take it from someone who built up a fictional universe for 15 years: World building is never over. You are giving us a barebones lore story and then say "Have fun". Thats lazy. You are not giving us a full fledged world, you are giving us random ideas that you somehow make it so they work together with no actual connecting parts,

So I've got two ideas that maybe would be kinda cool:  Firstly, the snowy mountains; I know this seems kind of out there, but maybe a society heavily inspired by Greek or Roman society. Think in the likes of Mount Olympus, just maybe a bit snowier than usually portrayed. There could be a dangerous ascent to the city of gods, with huge statues and other Greek/Roman architecture made of marble or the likes. The ascent should be very difficult, with parkour sections, pillager camps (that are also trying to make it to the top) and powerful mobs with ancient and powerful equipment. At the top, the city of gods await you, with beautiful architecture, libraries and telescopes (as the Greeks were very ahead and sophisticated for their time in history) and of course a colosseum, which if you manage to be victorious, you should be rewarded with a powerful trident or maybe a netherite helmet as it looks a bit like a roman soldier's helmet. Maybe the entrance to the end should also be here, as this is clearly an endgame area.    Secondly, the savannah; an underground society, inspired by the simple prairie dog. They hide underground to protect themselves from the dangers above, mainly ravagers. They are inspired by African tribal-society, valuing the hunt more than anything else. They therefore consist of fletchers and butchers, but their shamans(clerics) also have immense proficiency in potion brewing, as this connects them to their gods. Taking part in their hunting rituals, you could be tasked to hunt down and claim the trophies of certain mobs, rewarding you maybe a bow of some kind. For their architecture, I was imagining of course traditional (or exaggerated I suppose)  tribal-inspired dÃ©cor, like totem poles, clay idols, clay paintings and exotic animal skin. The layout could maybe be inspired a bit by skaven undercities blended with The Sunless City from Outer Wilds, of course a tribal aesthetic instead of skaven or nomai.   Hope this at least can be to at least a bit of inspiration!  :D

Here's an interesting way to write the tundra and pine forest biome: Maybe, long ago, there were two warring tribes in the pine forest, and a peace loving tribe in what is now the tundra. Both of the tribes in the forest saw the pacifist tribe as an easy target to get resources.  The peace loving tribe, who's now fighting a defensive war on two fronts, goes to the witches in the mushroom forest to beg for a way to make the warring tribes leave them alone. The witches use a powerful magical blizzard to freeze the area around the peace loving tribe to the point of being nearly inhospitable.  Now many years later, the survivors of the blizzard live as nomads, traveling around the tundra. These Eskimo-like people still hold on to the ways of their ancestors, but are very much prepared to answer hostility with overwhelming hostility.

As a person who lives in the west this is a pretty good looking town. Now for a history lesson. The town TrixyBlox built would be called a "boomtown" these towns were usually setup near or right next to the railroad. They also set these towns up that way they can the resources. These were commonly mined materials such as gold, silver, iron, coal, lead, and other materials seen as viable at the time. These towns would appear at almost at random simply BOOMING from nowhere. (hence the name boomtown) Now of course if you set up a town simply because it is close to materials and its the only reason the towns running then the town will likely end up dead in a few years. Some find other sources of income such as Phoenix the capital of Arizona. They survived by using the rivers and dams to make the land there farmable making it sustainable and hence it lives today. But some boomtowns would have survived cause they struck it lucky, a good example would be Silver city NM. The place was originally made to mine silver that was in the area. The main reason it still stands today with a healthy population is because the city is still mining materials (just ask my grandpa) although ironically finding silver is no longer happening and they instead find other valuable material.  And to those wondering why people whore leather in the west and its burning deserts its because it stopped plants to (if lucky) even some animals from going through your clothes and into your skin. Though the average person wore something a little bit lighter on the chest area that covered themselves though. Light soft material kept the sun from hitting yourself and this would stop you from getting even more hot.  If I made  any mistakes in my history lesson please let me know!
